      <p>
       <b>
        Google Earth
       </b>
       is a
       <a href="/wiki/Computer_program" title="Computer program">
        computer program
       </a>
       that renders a
       <a href="/wiki/3D_computer_graphics" title="3D computer graphics">
        3D
       </a>
       representation of
       <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">
        Earth
       </a>
       based on
       <a href="/wiki/Satellite_imagery" title="Satellite imagery">
        satellite imagery
       </a>
       . The program maps the Earth by
       <a href="/wiki/Superimposition" title="Superimposition">
        superimposing
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Satellite_imagery" title="Satellite imagery">
        satellite images
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Aerial_photography" title="Aerial photography">
        aerial photography
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Geographic_information_system" title="Geographic information system">
        GIS data
       </a>
       onto a
       <a href="/wiki/3D_computer_graphics" title="3D computer graphics">
        3D
       </a>
       globe, allowing users to see cities and landscapes from various angles. Users can explore the globe by entering addresses and coordinates, or by using a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Keyboard_(computing)" title="Keyboard (computing)">
        keyboard
       </a>
       or
       <a href="/wiki/Computer_mouse" title="Computer mouse">
        mouse
       </a>
       . The program can also be downloaded on a
       <a href="/wiki/Smartphone" title="Smartphone">
        smartphone
       </a>
       or
       <a href="/wiki/Tablet_computer" title="Tablet computer">
        tablet
       </a>
       , using a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Touch_screen" title="Touch screen">
        touch screen
       </a>
       or
       <a href="/wiki/Stylus" title="Stylus">
        stylus
       </a>
       to navigate. Users may use the program to add their own data using
       <a href="/wiki/Keyhole_Markup_Language" title="Keyhole Markup Language">
        Keyhole Markup Language
       </a>
       and upload them through various sources, such as forums or
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blogs" title="Blogs">
        blogs
       </a>
       . Google Earth is able to show various kinds of images overlaid on the surface of the earth and is also a
       <a href="/wiki/Web_Map_Service" title="Web Map Service">
        Web Map Service
       </a>
       client.
      </p>
      <p>
       In addition to Earth navigation, Google Earth provides a series of other tools through the desktop application. Additional globes for the
       <a href="/wiki/Moon" title="Moon">
        Moon
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Mars" title="Mars">
        Mars
       </a>
       are available, as well as a tool for viewing the
       <a href="/wiki/Night_sky" title="Night sky">
        night sky
       </a>
       . A
       <a href="/wiki/Flight_simulator" title="Flight simulator">
        flight simulator
       </a>
       game is also included. Other features allow users to view photos from various places uploaded to
       <a href="/wiki/Panoramio" title="Panoramio">
        Panoramio
       </a>
       , information provided by
       <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia" title="Wikipedia">
        Wikipedia
       </a>
       on some locations, and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Street_View" title="Street View">
        Street View
       </a>
       imagery. The web-based version of Google Earth also includes Voyager, a feature that periodically adds in-program tours, often presented by scientists and documentarians.
      </p>
      <p>
       Google Earth has been viewed by some as a threat to
       <a href="/wiki/Privacy" title="Privacy">
        privacy
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/National_security" title="National security">
        national security
       </a>
       , leading to the program being banned in multiple countries. Some countries have requested that certain areas be obscured in Google's satellite images, usually areas containing military facilities.
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

         <ul>
          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-3">

            <span class="tocnumber">
             2.1
            </span>
            <span class="toctext">
             3D imagery
            </span>

      <p>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
        History
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Google_Earth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Google Earth was originally developed by Keyhole, Inc., a
       <a href="/wiki/Mountain_View,_California" title="Mountain View, California">
        Mountain View
       </a>
       -based company founded in 2001. Keyhole, after being spun off from
       <a href="/wiki/Vicarious_Visions" title="Vicarious Visions">
        Intrinsic Graphics
       </a>
       , received funding from the
       <a href="/wiki/Central_Intelligence_Agency" title="Central Intelligence Agency">
        Central Intelligence Agency
       </a>
       's venture capital firm,
       <a href="/wiki/In-Q-Tel" title="In-Q-Tel">
        In-Q-Tel
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/National_Geospatial-Intelligence_Agency" title="National Geospatial-Intelligence Agency">
        National Geospatial-Intelligence Agency
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pandooakland_7-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-pandooakland-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       in addition to smaller capital from
       <a href="/wiki/Nvidia" title="Nvidia">
        Nvidia
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Sony" title="Sony">
        Sony
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Keyhole developed the program under the name
       <b>
        Keyhole EarthViewer
       </b>
       , and sold the product for uses in fields such as
       <a href="/wiki/Real_estate" title="Real estate">
        real estate
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Urban_planning" title="Urban planning">
        urban planning
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/War" title="War">
        defense
       </a>
       , and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Intelligence_(information_gathering)" title="Intelligence (information gathering)">
        intelligence
       </a>
       . Google acquired the company in 2004,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       driving public interest in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Geospatial" title="Geospatial">
        geospatial
       </a>
       technologies and applications.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Since then, Google has given the program a focus on exploration, with tours provided by humanitarian outreach programs, 3D modeling of hundreds of cities, and 3D globes of other planets.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Imagery">
        Imagery
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Google_Earth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Imagery">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Google Earth's imagery is displayed on a digital
       <a href="/wiki/Globe" title="Globe">
        globe
       </a>
       , which displays the planet's surface using a single composited image from a far distance. After zooming in far enough, the imagery transitions into different imagery of the same area with finer detail, which varies in date and time from one area to the next. The imagery is retrieved from
       <a href="/wiki/Satellite" title="Satellite">
        satellites
       </a>
       or
       <a href="/wiki/Aircraft" title="Aircraft">
        aircraft
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Before the launch of
       <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">
        NASA
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Geological_Survey" title="United States Geological Survey">
        USGS's
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Landsat_8" title="Landsat 8">
        Landsat 8
       </a>
       satellite, Google relied partially on imagery from
       <a href="/wiki/Landsat_7" title="Landsat 7">
        Landsat 7
       </a>
       , which suffered from a hardware malfunction that left diagonal gaps in images.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2013, Google used
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Datamining" title="Datamining">
        datamining
       </a>
       to remedy the issue, providing what was described as a successor to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blue_Marble" title="Blue Marble">
        Blue Marble
       </a>
       image of Earth, with a single large image of the entire planet. This was achieved by combining multiple sets of imagery taken from Landsat 7 to eliminate clouds and diagonal gaps, creating a single "mosaic" image.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Google now uses Landsat 8 to provide imagery in a higher quality and with greater frequency.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
        <a href="#cite_note-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Imagery is hosted on Google's servers, which are contacted by the application when opened, requiring an Internet connection.
      </p>
      <p>
       Imagery resolution ranges from 15 meters of resolution to 15 centimeters. For much of the Earth, Google Earth uses
       <a href="/wiki/Digital_elevation_model" title="Digital elevation model">
        digital elevation model
       </a>
       data collected by
       <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">
        NASA
       </a>
       's
       <a href="/wiki/Shuttle_Radar_Topography_Mission" title="Shuttle Radar Topography Mission">
        Shuttle Radar Topography Mission
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
        <a href="#cite_note-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This creates the impression of three-dimensional terrain, even where the imagery is only two-dimensional.
      </p>
      <p>
       <span id="Copyright">
       </span>
       Every image created from Google Earth using satellite data provided by Google Earth is a
       <a href="/wiki/Copyright" title="Copyright">
        copyrighted
       </a>
       map. Any derivative from Google Earth is made from copyrighted data which, under
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Copyright_Law" title="United States Copyright Law">
        United States Copyright Law
       </a>
       , may not be used except under the licenses Google provides. Google allows
       <a href="/wiki/Non-commercial" title="Non-commercial">
        non-commercial
       </a>
       personal use of the images (e.g. on a personal website or blog) as long as copyrights and attributions are preserved.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       By contrast, images created with NASA's globe software
       <a href="/wiki/NASA_World_Wind" title="NASA World Wind">
        World Wind
       </a>
       use
       <a href="/wiki/The_Blue_Marble" title="The Blue Marble">
        The Blue Marble
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Landsat" title="Landsat">
        Landsat
       </a>
       , or USGS imagery, each of which is in the
       <a href="/wiki/Public_domain" title="Public domain">
        public domain
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       <span id="historicalimagery">
       </span>
       In version 5.0, Google introduced Historical Imagery, allowing users to view earlier imagery. Clicking the
       <a href="/wiki/Clock" title="Clock">
        clock
       </a>
       icon in the toolbar opens a time slider, which marks the time of available imagery from the past. This feature allows for observation of an area's changes over time.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dive_into_New_Google_Earth_18-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Dive_into_New_Google_Earth-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="3D_imagery">
        3D imagery
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Google_Earth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 3D imagery">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:3D_locations_in_Google_Earth.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="736" data-file-width="1436" height="179" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/3D_locations_in_Google_Earth.png/350px-3D_locations_in_Google_Earth.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/3D_locations_in_Google_Earth.png/525px-3D_locations_in_Google_Earth.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/3D_locations_in_Google_Earth.png/700px-3D_locations_in_Google_Earth.png 2x" width="350"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:3D_locations_in_Google_Earth.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Countries with 3D coverage in Google Earth as of May 2015
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Google Earth shows
       <a href="/wiki/3D_computer_graphics" title="3D computer graphics">
        3D
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Building_model" title="Building model">
        building models
       </a>
       in some cities, including photorealistic 3D imagery. The first 3D buildings in Google Earth were created using
       <a href="/wiki/3D_modeling" title="3D modeling">
        3D modeling
       </a>
       applications such as
       <a href="/wiki/SketchUp" title="SketchUp">
        SketchUp
       </a>
       and, beginning in 2009,
       <a href="/wiki/Google_Building_Maker" title="Google Building Maker">
        Building Maker
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
        <a href="#cite_note-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and were uploaded to Google Earth via the
       <a href="/wiki/3D_Warehouse" title="3D Warehouse">
        3D Warehouse
       </a>
       . In June 2012, Google announced that it would be replacing user-generated 3D buildings with an auto-generated 3D mesh.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
        <a href="#cite_note-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This would be phased in, starting with select larger cities, with the notable exception of cities such as
       <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">
        London
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">
        Toronto
       </a>
       which required more time to process detailed imagery of their vast number of buildings. The reason given is to have greater uniformity in 3D buildings, and to compete with
       <a href="/wiki/Here_(company)" title="Here (company)">
        Nokia Here
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Apple_Maps" title="Apple Maps">
        Apple Maps
       </a>
       , which were already using this technology. The coverage began that year in 21 cities in four countries.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
        <a href="#cite_note-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
       By early 2016, 3D imagery had been expanded to hundreds of cities in over 40 countries, including every
       <a href="/wiki/U.S._state" title="U.S. state">
        U.S. state
       </a>
       and encompassing every continent except Antarctica.
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2009, in a collaboration between Google and the
       <a href="/wiki/Museo_del_Prado" title="Museo del Prado">
        Museo del Prado
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">
        Madrid
       </a>
       , the museum selected 14 of its paintings to be photographed and displayed at the resolution of 14,000
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Megapixel" title="Megapixel">
        megapixels
       </a>
       inside the 3D version of the Prado in Google Earth and
       <a href="/wiki/Google_Maps" title="Google Maps">
        Google Maps
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
        <a href="#cite_note-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
        <a href="#cite_note-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Street_View">
        Street View
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Google_Earth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Street View">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Google_Street_View" title="Google Street View">
        Google Street View
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       On April 15, 2008, with version 4.3, Google fully integrated
       <a href="/wiki/Google_Street_View" title="Google Street View">
        Street View
       </a>
       into Google Earth.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PCM4.3_24-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-PCM4.3-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Street View displays 360° panoramic street-level photos of select cities and their surroundings. The photos were taken by cameras mounted on automobiles, can be viewed at different scales and from many angles, and are navigable by arrow icons imposed on them.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Water_and_ocean">
        Water and ocean
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Google_Earth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Water and ocean">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Introduced in Google Earth 5.0 in 2009, the Google Ocean feature allows users to zoom below the surface of the ocean and view the 3D
       <a href="/wiki/Bathymetry" title="Bathymetry">
        bathymetry
       </a>
       . Supporting over 20 content layers, it contains information from leading scientists and
       <a href="/wiki/Oceanography" title="Oceanography">
        oceanographers
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
        <a href="#cite_note-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On April 14, 2009, Google added underwater terrain data for the
       <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes" title="Great Lakes">
        Great Lakes
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
        <a href="#cite_note-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
        <a href="#cite_note-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In June 2011, Google increased the resolution of some deep ocean floor areas from 1-kilometer grids to 100 meters.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
        <a href="#cite_note-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The high-resolution features were developed by oceanographers at Columbia University's Lamont-Doherty Earth Observatory from scientific data collected on research cruises. The sharper focus is available for about 5 percent of the oceans. This can be seen in the Hudson off New York City, the Wini Seamount near Hawaii, and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mendocino_Ridge" title="Mendocino Ridge">
        Mendocino Ridge
       </a>
       off the U.S Pacific coast.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
        <a href="#cite_note-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Outer_space">
        Outer space
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Google_Earth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Outer space">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Google_Earth_Mars.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="254" data-file-width="392" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9a/Google_Earth_Mars.png/220px-Google_Earth_Mars.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9a/Google_Earth_Mars.png/330px-Google_Earth_Mars.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/9/9a/Google_Earth_Mars.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Google_Earth_Mars.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A picture of
         <a href="/wiki/Mars" title="Mars">
          Mars
         </a>
         ' landscape
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Google_Earth_Sky.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="254" data-file-width="392" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/75/Google_Earth_Sky.png/220px-Google_Earth_Sky.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/75/Google_Earth_Sky.png/330px-Google_Earth_Sky.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/7/75/Google_Earth_Sky.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Google_Earth_Sky.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Google Earth in Sky Viewing Mode
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Google_moon_1.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="253" data-file-width="393" height="142" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f5/Google_moon_1.jpg/220px-Google_moon_1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f5/Google_moon_1.jpg/330px-Google_moon_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/f/f5/Google_moon_1.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Google_moon_1.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         One of the lunar landers viewed in Google Moon
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Google Earth can be used as a program to view
       <a href="/wiki/Outer_space" title="Outer space">
        outer space
       </a>
       , including the surfaces of various objects in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Solar_system" title="Solar system">
        solar system
       </a>
       . Google has programs and features, including within Google Earth, allowing exploration of
       <a href="/wiki/Mars" title="Mars">
        Mars
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Moon" title="Moon">
        moon
       </a>
       , and the view of the sky from Earth.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Google_Sky">
        Google Sky
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Google_Earth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Google Sky">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Google Sky is a feature that was introduced in Google Earth 4.2 on August 22, 2007, in a browser-based application on March 13, 2008,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
        <a href="#cite_note-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and to
       <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">
        Android
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Smartphones" title="Smartphones">
        smartphones
       </a>
       , with
       <a href="/wiki/Augmented_reality" title="Augmented reality">
        augmented reality
       </a>
       features. Google Sky allows users to view
       <a href="/wiki/Star" title="Star">
        stars
       </a>
       and other
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Celestial_bodies" title="Celestial bodies">
        celestial bodies
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
        <a href="#cite_note-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It was produced by
       <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">
        Google
       </a>
       through a partnership with the
       <a href="/wiki/Space_Telescope_Science_Institute" title="Space Telescope Science Institute">
        Space Telescope Science Institute
       </a>
       (STScI) in Baltimore, the science operations center for the
       <a href="/wiki/Hubble_Space_Telescope" title="Hubble Space Telescope">
        Hubble Space Telescope
       </a>
       . Dr.
       <a href="/wiki/Alberto_Conti" title="Alberto Conti">
        Alberto Conti
       </a>
       and his co-developer Dr. Carol Christian of STScI plan to add the public images from 2007,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
        <a href="#cite_note-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
       as well as color images of all of the archived data from Hubble's Advanced Camera for Surveys. Newly released
       <a href="/wiki/Hubble_Space_Telescope" title="Hubble Space Telescope">
        Hubble
       </a>
       pictures will be added to the Google Sky program as soon as they are issued.
      </p>
      <p>
       New features such as multi-wavelength data, positions of major satellites and their orbits as well as educational resources will be provided to the Google Earth community and also through Christian and Conti's website for Sky.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
        <a href="#cite_note-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Also visible on Sky mode are constellations, stars, galaxies, and animations depicting the planets in their orbits. A real-time Google Sky
       <a href="/wiki/Mashup_(web_application_hybrid)" title="Mashup (web application hybrid)">
        mashup
       </a>
       of recent astronomical transients, using the
       <a href="/wiki/VOEvent" title="VOEvent">
        VOEvent
       </a>
       protocol, is being provided by the VOEventNet collaboration.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
        <a href="#cite_note-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Other programs similar to Google Sky include
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Microsoft_WorldWide_Telescope" title="Microsoft WorldWide Telescope">
        Microsoft WorldWide Telescope
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Stellarium_(software)" title="Stellarium (software)">
        Stellarium
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Google_Mars">
        Google Mars
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Google_Earth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Google Mars">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Google Mars is an application within Google Earth that is a version of the program for imagery of the planet Mars. Google also operates a browser-based version, although the maps are of a much higher resolution within Google Earth, and include 3D terrain, as well as
       <a href="/wiki/Infrared" title="Infrared">
        infrared
       </a>
       imagery and elevation data. There are also some extremely-high-resolution images from the
       <a href="/wiki/Mars_Reconnaissance_Orbiter" title="Mars Reconnaissance Orbiter">
        Mars Reconnaissance Orbiter
       </a>
       's
       <a href="/wiki/HiRISE" title="HiRISE">
        HiRISE
       </a>
       camera that are of a similar resolution to those of the cities on Earth. Finally, there are many high-resolution panoramic images from various Mars landers, such as the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mars_Exploration_Rovers" title="Mars Exploration Rovers">
        Mars Exploration Rovers
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spirit_Rover" title="Spirit Rover">
        Spirit
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Opportunity_Rover" title="Opportunity Rover">
        Opportunity
       </a>
       , that can be viewed in a similar way to
       <a href="/wiki/Google_Street_View" title="Google Street View">
        Google Street View
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Mars also has a small application found near the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Face_on_Mars" title="Face on Mars">
        face on Mars
       </a>
       . It is called Meliza, a robot character the user can speak with.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
        <a href="#cite_note-35">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Google_Moon">
        Google Moon
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Google_Earth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Google Moon">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Originally a browser application, Google Moon is a feature that allows exploration of the moon. Google brought the feature to Google Earth for the 40th anniversary of the
       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_11" title="Apollo 11">
        Apollo 11
       </a>
       mission on July 20, 2009.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
        <a href="#cite_note-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It was announced and demonstrated to a group of invited guests by Google along with
       <a href="/wiki/Buzz_Aldrin" title="Buzz Aldrin">
        Buzz Aldrin
       </a>
       at the
       <a href="/wiki/Newseum" title="Newseum">
        Newseum
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">
        Washington, D.C.
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
        <a href="#cite_note-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
        <a href="#cite_note-38">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Google Moon includes several tours, including one for the
       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_program" title="Apollo program">
        Apollo missions
       </a>
       , incorporating maps, videos, and Street View-style panoramas, all provided by NASA.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Other_features">
        Other features
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Google_Earth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Other features">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Google Earth has numerous features which allow the user to learn about specific places. These are called "layers", and include different forms of media, including photo and video. Some layers include tours, which guide the user between specific places in a set order. Layers are created using the
       <a href="/wiki/Keyhole_Markup_Language" title="Keyhole Markup Language">
        Keyhole Markup Language
       </a>
       , or KML, which users can also use to create customized layers.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
        <a href="#cite_note-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Locations can be marked with placemarks and organized in folders; For example, a user can use placemarks to list interesting landmarks around the globe, then provide a description with photos and videos, which can be viewed by clicking on the placemarks while viewing the new layer in the application.
      </p>
      <p>
       In December 2006, Google Earth added a new integration with
       <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia" title="Wikipedia">
        Wikipedia
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Panoramio" title="Panoramio">
        Panoramio
       </a>
       . For the Wikipedia layer, entries are
       <a href="/wiki/Web_scraping" title="Web scraping">
        scraped
       </a>
       for coordinates via the
       <a href="/wiki/Template:Coord" title="Template:Coord">
        Coord templates
       </a>
       . There is also a community-layer from the project
       <a class="extiw" href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProjekt_Georeferenzierung/Wikipedia-World/en" title="de:Wikipedia:WikiProjekt Georeferenzierung/Wikipedia-World/en">
        Wikipedia-World
       </a>
       . More coordinates are used, different types are in the display, and different languages are supported than the built-in Wikipedia layer.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
        <a href="#cite_note-40">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
        <a href="#cite_note-41">
         [41]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Panoramio layer features pictures uploaded by Panoramio users, placed in Google Earth based off user-provided location data. In addition to flat images, Google Earth also includes a layer for user-submitted panoramic photos, navigable in a similar way to Street View.
      </p>
      <p>
       Google Earth includes multiple features that allow the user to monitor current events. In 2007, Google began offering users the ability to monitor traffic data provided by
       <a href="/wiki/Google_Traffic" title="Google Traffic">
        Google Traffic
       </a>
       in real time, based on information
       <a href="/wiki/Crowdsourcing" title="Crowdsourcing">
        crowdsourced
       </a>
       from the GPS-identified locations of cell phone users.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
        <a href="#cite_note-42">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Flight_simulators">
        Flight simulators
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Google_Earth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Flight simulators">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Toronto_downtown.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="227" data-file-width="439" height="114" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a3/Toronto_downtown.png/220px-Toronto_downtown.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a3/Toronto_downtown.png/330px-Toronto_downtown.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/a/a3/Toronto_downtown.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Toronto_downtown.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Toronto" title="Downtown Toronto">
          Downtown Toronto
         </a>
         as seen from an
         <a href="/wiki/General_Dynamics_F-16_Fighting_Falcon" title="General Dynamics F-16 Fighting Falcon">
          F-16 Fighting Falcon
         </a>
         during a simulated flight
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In Google Earth 4.2, a
       <a href="/wiki/Flight_simulator" title="Flight simulator">
        flight simulator
       </a>
       was added to the application. It was originally a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Easter_egg_(virtual)#Software-based" title="Easter egg (virtual)">
        hidden feature
       </a>
       when introduced in 2007, but starting with 4.3, it was given a labeled option in the menu. In addition to keyboard control, the simulator can be controlled with a mouse or joystick. The flight simulator can be commanded with the keyboard, mouse, or plugged-in joystick.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">
        <a href="#cite_note-43">
         [43]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
        <a href="#cite_note-44">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The simulator also runs with animation, allowing objects such as planes to animate while on the simulator.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
        <a href="#cite_note-45">
         [45]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Another flight simulator,
       <a href="/wiki/GeoFS" title="GeoFS">
        GeoFS
       </a>
       , was created under the name GEFS-Online using the Google Earth Plug-in API to operate within a
       <a href="/wiki/Web_browser" title="Web browser">
        web browser
       </a>
       . As of September 1, 2015, the program now uses the open-source program CesiumJS, due to the Google Earth Plug-in being discontinued.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
        <a href="#cite_note-46">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Liquid_Galaxy">
        Liquid Galaxy
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Google_Earth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Liquid Galaxy">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Liquid_Galaxy" title="Liquid Galaxy">
        Liquid Galaxy
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Liquid Galaxy is a cluster of computers running Google Earth creating an
       <a href="/wiki/Immersive_technology" title="Immersive technology">
        immersive experience
       </a>
       . On September 30, 2010, Google made the configuration and schematics for their rigs public,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
        <a href="#cite_note-47">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
       placing code and setup guides on the Liquid Galaxy wiki.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
        <a href="#cite_note-48">
         [48]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Liquid Galaxy has also been used as a panoramic photo viewer using KRpano, as well as a Google Street View viewer using Peruse-a-Rue
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
        <a href="#cite_note-49">
         [49]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Peruse-a-Rue is a method for synchronizing multiple Maps API clients.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
        <a href="#cite_note-50">
         [50]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Versions">
        Versions
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Google_Earth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Versions">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Google Earth has been released on
       <a href="/wiki/MacOS" title="MacOS">
        macOS
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Linux" title="Linux">
        Linux
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IOS_(Apple)" title="IOS (Apple)">
        iOS
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">
        Android
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Linux" title="Linux">
        Linux
       </a>
       version began with the version 4 beta of Google Earth, as a native port using the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Qt_(toolkit)" title="Qt (toolkit)">
        Qt toolkit
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Free_Software_Foundation" title="Free Software Foundation">
        Free Software Foundation
       </a>
       consider the development of a free compatible client for Google Earth to be a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/High_Priority_Free_Software_Projects" title="High Priority Free Software Projects">
        High Priority Free Software Project
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
        <a href="#cite_note-51">
         [51]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Google Earth was released for Android on February 22, 2010,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
        <a href="#cite_note-52">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and on iOS on October 27, 2008.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
        <a href="#cite_note-53">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
        <a href="#cite_note-54">
         [54]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The mobile versions of Google Earth can make use of
       <a href="/wiki/Multi-touch" title="Multi-touch">
        multi-touch
       </a>
       interfaces to move on the globe, zoom or rotate the view, and allow to select the current location. An automotive version of Google Earth was made available in the 2010
       <a href="/wiki/Audi_A8" title="Audi A8">
        Audi A8
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
        <a href="#cite_note-55">
         [55]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>

        </td>

        </td>
        <td>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>

          </li>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Google_Earth_Pro">
        Google Earth Pro
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Google_Earth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Google Earth Pro">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:246px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Google_Earth.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="406" data-file-width="244" height="406" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/0/0b/Google_Earth.png" width="244"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Google_Earth.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Google Earth running on
         <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">
          Android
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Google Earth Pro was originally the business-oriented upgrade to Google Earth, with features such as a movie maker and data importer. Up until late January 2015, it was available for $399/year, though Google decided to make it free to the public.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
        <a href="#cite_note-56">
         [56]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
        <a href="#cite_note-57">
         [57]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Google Earth Pro is currently the standard version of the Google Earth desktop application as of version 7.3.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
        <a href="#cite_note-58">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Pro version includes add-on software for movie making, advanced printing, and precise measurements, and is currently available for Windows, macOS 10.4 or later, and Linux.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
        <a href="#cite_note-59">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Google_Earth_Plus">
        Google Earth Plus
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Google_Earth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Google Earth Plus">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Discontinued in December 2008, Google Earth Plus was a paid subscription upgrade to Google Earth that provided customers with the following features, most of which have become available in the free Google Earth.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
        <a href="#cite_note-60">
         [60]
        </a>
       </sup>
       One such feature was
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GPS" title="GPS">
        GPS
       </a>
       integration, which allowed users to read tracks and waypoints from a
       <a href="/wiki/Global_Positioning_System" title="Global Positioning System">
        GPS
       </a>
       device. A variety of third-party applications have been created which provide this functionality using the basic version of Google Earth by generating KML or KMZ files based on user-specified or user-recorded waypoints.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Google_Earth_Enterprise">
        Google Earth Enterprise
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Google_Earth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Google Earth Enterprise">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Google Earth Enterprise is designed for use by organizations whose businesses could take advantage of the program's capabilities, for example by having a globe that holds company data available for anyone in that company.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
        <a href="#cite_note-61">
         [61]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As of March 20, 2015, Google has retired the Google Earth Enterprise product, with support ended March 22, 2017.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
        <a href="#cite_note-62">
         [62]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Google Earth Enterprise allowed developers to create maps and 3D globes for private use, and host them through the platform. GEE Fusion, GEE Server, and GEE Portable Server source code was published on GitHub under the Apache2 license in March 2017.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
        <a href="#cite_note-63">
         [63]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Google_Earth_9">
        Google Earth 9
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Google_Earth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Google Earth 9">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Google Earth 9 is a version of Google Earth first released on April 18, 2017, having been in development for two years.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
        <a href="#cite_note-64">
         [64]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The main feature of this version was the launching of a new web version of Google Earth, which is currently only available for
       <a href="/wiki/Google_Chrome" title="Google Chrome">
        Google Chrome
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_65-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:1-65">
         [65]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This version added the "Voyager" feature, whereby users can view a portal page containing guided tours led by scientists and documentarians.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_66-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:0-66">
         [66]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The version also added an "I'm Feeling Lucky" button, represented by a die, which takes the user to a random location on earth along with showing them a "Knowledge Card" containing a short excerpt from the location's Wikipedia article.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_66-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-:0-66">
         [66]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Google_Earth_Plug-in">
        Google Earth Plug-in
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Google_Earth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Google Earth Plug-in">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The Google Earth API was a free beta service, allowing users place a version of Google Earth into web pages. The API enabled sophisticated 3D map applications to be built.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
        <a href="#cite_note-67">
         [67]
        </a>
       </sup>
       At its unveiling at Google's 2008 I/O developer conference, the company showcased potential applications such as a game where the player controlled a milktruck atop a Google Earth surface.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
        <a href="#cite_note-68">
         [68]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Google Earth API has been deprecated as of December 15, 2014 and remained supported until December 15, 2015.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">
        <a href="#cite_note-69">
         [69]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Google Chrome ended support for the
       <a href="/wiki/NPAPI" title="NPAPI">
        Netscape Plugin API
       </a>
       (which the Google Earth API relies on) by the end of 2016.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
        <a href="#cite_note-70">
         [70]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Google_Earth_VR">
        Google Earth VR
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Google_Earth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Google Earth VR">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       On November 16, 2016, Google released a
       <a href="/wiki/Virtual_reality" title="Virtual reality">
        virtual reality
       </a>
       version of Google Earth for
       <a href="/wiki/Valve_Corporation" title="Valve Corporation">
        Valve's
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Steam_(software)" title="Steam (software)">
        Steam
       </a>
       computer gaming platform.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">
        <a href="#cite_note-71">
         [71]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
        <a href="#cite_note-72">
         [72]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Google Earth VR allows users to navigate using VR controllers, and is currently compatible with the
       <a href="/wiki/Oculus_Rift" title="Oculus Rift">
        Oculus Rift
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/HTC_Vive" title="HTC Vive">
        HTC Vive
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Virtual_reality_headsets" title="Virtual reality headsets">
        virtual reality headsets
       </a>
       . On September 14, 2017, as part of Google Earth VR's 1.4 update, Google added Street View support.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
        <a href="#cite_note-73">
         [73]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Google_Earth_Outreach">
        Google Earth Outreach
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Google_Earth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Google Earth Outreach">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       <b>
        Google Earth Outreach
       </b>
       is a charity program, through which Google promotes and donates to various non-profit organizations. Beginning in 2007, donations are often accompanied by layers featured in Google Earth, allowing users to view a non-profit's projects and goals by navigating to certain related locations.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
        <a href="#cite_note-74">
         [74]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Google Earth Outreach offers online training on using Google Earth and Google Maps for public education on issues affecting local regions or the entire globe. In June 2008, training was given to 20 indigenous tribes in the Amazon rainforest, such as the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paiter_people" title="Paiter people">
        Suruí
       </a>
       , to help them preserve their culture and raise awareness for the problem of deforestation.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
        <a href="#cite_note-75">
         [75]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Non-profit organizations featured in Google Earth via the Outreach program include
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arkive" title="Arkive">
        Arkive
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Global_Heritage_Fund" title="Global Heritage Fund">
        Global Heritage Fund
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/WaterAid" title="WaterAid">
        WaterAid
       </a>
       , and the
       <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Fund_for_Nature" title="World Wide Fund for Nature">
        World Wide Fund for Nature
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">
        <a href="#cite_note-76">
         [76]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
        <a href="#cite_note-77">
         [77]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Google_Earth_Engine">
        Google Earth Engine
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Google_Earth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Google Earth Engine">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       <b>
        Google Earth Engine
       </b>
       is a
       <a href="/wiki/Cloud_computing" title="Cloud computing">
        cloud computing
       </a>
       platform for processing
       <a href="/wiki/Satellite_imagery" title="Satellite imagery">
        satellite imagery
       </a>
       and other geospatial and observation data. It provides access to a large database of satellite imagery and the computational power needed to analyze those images.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Timothy_Gardner_78-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Timothy_Gardner-78">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Google Earth Engine allows observation of dynamic changes in agriculture, natural resources, and climate using geospatial data from the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Landsat" title="Landsat">
        Landsat
       </a>
       satellite program, which
       <a href="/wiki/Ground_track" title="Ground track">
        passes over
       </a>
       the same places on the Earth every sixteen days.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-googleearthengine_79-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-googleearthengine-79">
         [79]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
        <a href="#cite_note-80">
         [80]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Google Earth Engine has become a platform that makes Landsat data easily accessible to researchers.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-googleearthengine_79-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-googleearthengine-79">
         [79]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Google Earth Engine provides a data catalog along with computers for analysis; this allows scientists to collaborate using data, algorithms, and visualizations.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
        <a href="#cite_note-81">
         [81]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Google Earth Engine has been used multiple times as a tool for tracking
       <a href="/wiki/Deforestation" title="Deforestation">
        deforestation
       </a>
       . Initial applications of the engine have included mapping the forests of
       <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">
        Mexico
       </a>
       , identifying water in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Congo_basin" title="Congo basin">
        Congo basin
       </a>
       , and detecting deforestation in the
       <a href="/wiki/Amazon_rainforest" title="Amazon rainforest">
        Amazon rainforest
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Antonio_Regalado_82-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Antonio_Regalado-82">
         [82]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Using the Google Earth Engine to track global forest loss or gain, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_of_Maryland" title="University of Maryland">
        University of Maryland
       </a>
       reported an overall loss in global forest cover.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">
        <a href="#cite_note-83">
         [83]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Mellon_University" title="Carnegie Mellon University">
        Carnegie Institute for Science’s
       </a>
       CLASlite system and
       <a href="/wiki/Imazon" title="Imazon">
        Imazon
       </a>
       ’s Sisteme de Alerta de Deforesation (SAD) are two institutions that partnered with Google in the development of Google Earth Engine. Both organizations use the program to build maps of forests that measure environmental disturbances.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">
        <a href="#cite_note-84">
         [84]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Controversy_and_criticism">
        Controversy and criticism
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Google_Earth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Controversy and criticism">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Satellite_map_images_with_missing_or_unclear_data" title="Satellite map images with missing or unclear data">
        Satellite map images with missing or unclear data
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The software has been criticized by a number of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Special_interest_group" title="Special interest group">
        special interest groups
       </a>
       , including national officials, as being an
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Invasion_of_privacy" title="Invasion of privacy">
        invasion of privacy
       </a>
       or posing a threat to
       <a href="/wiki/National_security" title="National security">
        national security
       </a>
       . The typical argument is that the software provides information about military or other critical installations that could be used by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Terrorist" title="Terrorist">
        terrorists
       </a>
       . Google Earth has been blocked by Google in Iran
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iranban_85-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-iranban-85">
         [85]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and Sudan
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sudanban_86-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-sudanban-86">
         [86]
        </a>
       </sup>
       since 2007, due to United States government export restrictions. The program has also been blocked in Morocco since 2006 by Maroc Telecom, a major service provider in the country.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morocco_censorship_87-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Morocco_censorship-87">
         [87]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Royal_Stables.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="256" data-file-width="389" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/68/Royal_Stables.jpg/220px-Royal_Stables.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/68/Royal_Stables.jpg/330px-Royal_Stables.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/6/68/Royal_Stables.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Royal_Stables.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Blurred out image of the Royal Stables in
         <a href="/wiki/The_Hague" title="The Hague">
          The Hague
         </a>
         , Netherlands. This has since been partially lifted.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In the academic realm, increasing attention has been devoted to both Google Earth and its place in the development of digital globes. In particular, the International Journal of Digital Earth features multiple articles evaluating and comparing the development Google Earth and its differences when compared to other professional, scientific, and governmental platforms.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
        <a href="#cite_note-88">
         [88]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Google Earth's role in the expansion of "earth observing media" has been examined for its role in shaping a shared cultural consciousness regarding climate change and humanity's capacity to treat the earth as an engineerable object.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
        <a href="#cite_note-89">
         [89]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Defense">
        Defense
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Google_Earth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Defense">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <ul>
       <li>
        In 2006, one user spotted a large topographical replica in a remote region of China. The model is a small-scale (1/500) version of the
        <a href="/wiki/Karakoram" title="Karakoram">
         Karakoram
        </a>
        Mountain Range, which is under the control of China but claimed by India. When later confirmed as a replica of this region, spectators began entertaining military implications.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SMHChinaModel_90-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-SMHChinaModel-90">
          [90]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IndianExpressChinaModel_91-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-IndianExpressChinaModel-91">
          [91]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        In July 2007, it was reported that a new
        <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Liberation_Army_Navy" title="People's Liberation Army Navy">
         Chinese Navy
        </a>
        <a href="/wiki/Type_094_submarine" title="Type 094 submarine">
         Jin-class
        </a>
        <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_weapon" title="Nuclear weapon">
         nuclear
        </a>
        <a href="/wiki/Ballistic_missile" title="Ballistic missile">
         ballistic missile
        </a>
        <a href="/wiki/Submarine" title="Submarine">
         submarine
        </a>
        was photographed at the Xiaopingdao Submarine Base south of
        <a href="/wiki/Dalian" title="Dalian">
         Dalian
        </a>
        .
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">
         <a href="#cite_note-92">
          [92]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Hamas" title="Hamas">
         Hamas
        </a>
        and the
        <a href="/wiki/Al-Aqsa_Martyrs%27_Brigades" title="Al-Aqsa Martyrs' Brigades">
         al-Aqsa Martyrs' Brigades
        </a>
        have reportedly used Google Earth to plan
        <a href="/wiki/Qassam_rocket" title="Qassam rocket">
         Qassam rocket
        </a>
        attacks on Israel from Gaza (See:
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Qassam_rocket_attacks" title="List of Qassam rocket attacks">
         List of Qassam rocket attacks
        </a>
        .)
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
         <a href="#cite_note-93">
          [93]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">
         <a href="#cite_note-94">
          [94]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="National_security">
        National security
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Google_Earth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: National security">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Former
        <a href="/wiki/President_of_India" title="President of India">
         President
        </a>
        of India
        <a href="/wiki/A._P._J._Abdul_Kalam" title="A. P. J. Abdul Kalam">
         A. P. J. Abdul Kalam
        </a>
        expressed concern over the availability of high-resolution pictures of sensitive locations in India.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IndianPresCrit_95-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-IndianPresCrit-95">
          [95]
         </a>
        </sup>
        Google subsequently agreed to censor such sites.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">
         <a href="#cite_note-96">
          [96]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Indian_Space_Research_Organisation" title="Indian Space Research Organisation">
         Indian Space Research Organisation
        </a>
        said Google Earth poses a security threat to India, and seeks dialogue with Google officials.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ISROCrit_97-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-ISROCrit-97">
          [97]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">
         South Korean
        </a>
        government expressed concern that the software offers images of the
        <a href="/wiki/Blue_House" title="Blue House">
         presidential palace
        </a>
        and various military installations that could possibly be used by hostile neighbor
        <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">
         North Korea
        </a>
        .
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SouthKoreaGovCrit_98-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-SouthKoreaGovCrit-98">
          [98]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        In 2006, Google Earth began offering detailed images of classified areas in Israel. The images showed
        <a href="/wiki/Israel_Defense_Forces" title="Israel Defense Forces">
         Israel Defense Forces
        </a>
        bases, including secret
        <a href="/wiki/Israeli_Air_Force" title="Israeli Air Force">
         Israeli Air Force
        </a>
        facilities, Israel's
        <a href="/wiki/Arrow_(Israeli_missile)" title="Arrow (Israeli missile)">
         Arrow missile
        </a>
        defense system, military headquarters and Defense Ministry compound in
        <a href="/wiki/Tel_Aviv" title="Tel Aviv">
         Tel Aviv
        </a>
        , a top-secret power station near
        <a href="/wiki/Ashkelon" title="Ashkelon">
         Ashkelon
        </a>
        , and the
        <a href="/wiki/Negev_Nuclear_Research_Center" title="Negev Nuclear Research Center">
         Negev Nuclear Research Center
        </a>
        . Also shown was the alleged headquarters of the
        <a href="/wiki/Mossad" title="Mossad">
         Mossad
        </a>
        , Israel's foreign intelligence service, whose location is highly classified.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">
         <a href="#cite_note-99">
          [99]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">
         <a href="#cite_note-100">
          [100]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        As a result of pressure from the
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_government" title="United States government">
         United States government
        </a>
        , the residence of the
        <a href="/wiki/Vice_President_of_the_United_States" title="Vice President of the United States">
         Vice President
        </a>
        at
        <a href="/wiki/Number_One_Observatory_Circle" title="Number One Observatory Circle">
         Number One Observatory Circle
        </a>
        was obscured through
        <a href="/wiki/Pixelization" title="Pixelization">
         pixelization
        </a>
        in Google Earth and
        <a href="/wiki/Google_Maps" title="Google Maps">
         Google Maps
        </a>
        in 2006, but this restriction has since been lifted. The usefulness of this downgrade is questionable, as high-resolution photos and aerial surveys of the property are readily available on the Internet elsewhere.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101">
         <a href="#cite_note-101">
          [101]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <a href="/wiki/Capitol_Hill" title="Capitol Hill">
         Capitol Hill
        </a>
        also used to be pixelized in this way. The Royal Stables in
        <a href="/wiki/The_Hague" title="The Hague">
         The Hague
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">
         Netherlands
        </a>
        also used to be pixelized, and are still pixelized at high zoom levels.
       </li>
       <li>
        The lone surviving gunman involved in the
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/November_2008_Mumbai_attacks" title="November 2008 Mumbai attacks">
         2008 Mumbai attacks
        </a>
        admitted to using Google Earth to familiarise himself with the locations of buildings used in the attacks.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">
         <a href="#cite_note-102">
          [102]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Michael_Finton" title="Michael Finton">
         Michael Finton
        </a>
        , aka Talib Islam, used Google Earth in planning his attempted September 24, 2009, bombing of the Paul Findley Federal Building and the adjacent offices of Congressman
        <a href="/wiki/Aaron_Schock" title="Aaron Schock">
         Aaron Schock
        </a>
        in
        <a href="/wiki/Springfield,_Illinois" title="Springfield, Illinois">
         Springfield, Illinois
        </a>
        .
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">
         <a href="#cite_note-103">
          [103]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Other_concerns">
        Other concerns
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Google_Earth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Other concerns">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Operators of the
        <a href="/wiki/Open-pool_Australian_lightwater_reactor" title="Open-pool Australian lightwater reactor">
         Lucas Heights nuclear reactor
        </a>
        in
        <a href="/wiki/Sydney" title="Sydney">
         Sydney
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/New_South_Wales" title="New South Wales">
         New South Wales
        </a>
        , Australia asked Google to censor high-resolution pictures of the facility.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ABCAUNukeFears_104-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-ABCAUNukeFears-104">
          [104]
         </a>
        </sup>
        They later withdrew the request.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SearchViewsAussieNukeReqDropped_105-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-SearchViewsAussieNukeReqDropped-105">
          [105]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        In 2009, Google superimposed old
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Woodblock_prints" title="Woodblock prints">
         woodblock prints
        </a>
        of maps from 18th and 19th century Japan over Japan today. These maps marked areas inhabited by the
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Burakumin" title="Burakumin">
          burakumin
         </a>
        </i>
        caste, who were considered "non-humans" for their "dirty" occupations, including
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leather_tanning" title="Leather tanning">
         leather tanning
        </a>
        and
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Butchery" title="Butchery">
         butchery
        </a>
        . Descendants of members of the burakumin caste still face discrimination today and many Japanese people feared that some would use these areas, labeled
        <i>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Etamura" title="Etamura">
          etamura
         </a>
        </i>
        (穢多村,
        <i>
         translation: "village of an abundance of defilement""
        </i>
        ), to target current inhabitants of them. These maps are still visible on Google Earth, but with the label removed where necessary.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106">
         <a href="#cite_note-106">
          [106]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        Late 2000s versions of Google Earth require a software component running in the background that will automatically download and install updates. Several users expressed concerns that there is not an easy way to disable this updater, as it runs without the permission of the user.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107">
         <a href="#cite_note-107">
          [107]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>

         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-9">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">

           </a>

           <span class="reference-accessdate">

            <span class="nowrap">

            </span>
            2017
           </span>
           .
          </cite>
          <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Google+Acquires+Keyhole&amp;rft.pub=Wall+Street+Journal&amp;rft.date=2004-10-27&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.wsj.com%2Farticles%2FSB109888284313557107&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGoogle+Earth">
